## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics / materials constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: Stress (sigma) is a function of strain (epsilon) and temperature (T), which is a core problem in mechanical behavior of materials. The relationships range from linear elasticity to nonlinear plasticity, thermal softening, and creep, often involving separable strain hardening and thermal activation terms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elasticity)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (plastic strain hardening, Hollomon equation)
- Temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = c0 * (1 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear thermal effect on elastic modulus)
- Thermal expansion stress: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * T) (thermal strain offset)
- Thermal softening exponential: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (separable strain hardening and thermal softening)
- Power-law thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (power-law separable form)
- Offset strain hardening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * T**c3 (yield offset with power-law hardening and thermal scaling)
- Kocks-Mecking type saturation: sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(-c2 * epsilon) + c3 * T (exponential saturation of hardening with thermal shift)
- Johnson-Cook inspired: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T) (strain hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Exponential strain hardening: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * epsilon) * T**c2 (exponential hardening with power-law thermal scaling)
- Logarithmic hardening: sigma = c0 * log(epsilon + c1) * exp(c2 * T) (log saturation at large strains, thermally activated)
- Quadratic elastic-plastic: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * T (nonlinear elasticity with linear thermal effect)
- Temperature shift factor: sigma = c0 * epsilon / (1 + c1 * T) (inverse thermal softening via rational function)
- Sigmoidal strain saturation: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 / (epsilon**c1 + c2) + c3 * T (strain hardening saturation with temperature offset)
- Sin-hyperbolic hardening: sigma = c0 * sinh(c1 * epsilon) * T**c2 (symmetric hardening with power-law thermal scaling)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear sigma-epsilon relationship indicates elastic (reversible) deformation.
- Power-law with exponent <1 (epsilon**c) models typical plastic strain hardening with diminishing rate.
- Exponential dependence on T (exp(c*T) or exp(c/T)) suggests thermally activated processes like creep or viscosity.
- Separable product form f(epsilon)*g(T) indicates the assumption of independent strain and temperature effects, common in phenomenological constitutive models.
- Additive term like epsilon - c*T reflects thermal expansion/contraction offset in stress.
- Rational saturation form epsilon**n/(epsilon**n + c) captures approach to a saturated stress level (dynamic recovery).
- Negative coefficient in T term (e.g., (1 - c*T)) indicates thermal softening.
- Logarithmic strain term log(epsilon+c) models stage III/IV hardening with saturation at large strains.
- Hyperbolic sine or similar transcendental functions may capture high strain-rate or stress sensitivity.
- Polynomial combination of epsilon with T scaling can approximate nonlinear thermo-elastic-plastic response within limited strain/temperature ranges.
